          --mr-toggled-font-family: Monospace;
        }
        .container-issue {
          width: 100%;

Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

Summary



<span class="line"><!---->Summary<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





A use-after-free vulnerability exists in the WebAudio blink::EventListenerMap functionality of Google Chrome Canary Build 96.0.4660.0 (64-bit) and Chromium 96.0.4660.0 (Build) (64-bit). A specially-crafted web page can lead to a use-after-free. An attacker can create special website to trigger this vulnerability.



<span class="line"><!---->A use-after-free vulnerability exists in the WebAudio blink::EventListenerMap functionality of Google Chrome Canary Build 96.0.4660.0 (64-bit) and Chromium 96.0.4660.0 (Build) (64-bit). A specially-crafted web page can lead to a use-after-free. An attacker can create special website to trigger this vulnerability.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Tested Versions



<span class="line"><!---->Tested Versions<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Google Chrome 95.0.4638.54 (Stable) 



<span class="line"><!---->Google Chrome 95.0.4638.54 (Stable) <!----></span>



<br>





Google Chrome Canary Build 96.0.4660.0 (64-bit) 



<span class="line"><!---->Google Chrome Canary Build 96.0.4660.0 (64-bit) <!----></span>



<br>





Google Chrome Chromium 96.0.4660.0 (Build) (64-bit)



<span class="line"><!---->Google Chrome Chromium 96.0.4660.0 (Build) (64-bit)<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Product URLs



<span class="line"><!---->Product URLs<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





https://www.google.com/chrome/



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://www.google.com/chrome/"><!---->https://www.google.com/chrome/<!----></a>



<br>



<br>





CVSSv3 Score



<span class="line"><!---->CVSSv3 Score<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





8.8 - CVSS:3.0/AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:R/S:U/C:H/I:H/A:H



<span class="line"><!---->8.8 - CVSS:3.0/AV:N/AC:L/PR:N/UI:R/S:U/C:H/I:H/A:H<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





CWE



<span class="line"><!---->CWE<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





CWE-416 - Use After Free



<span class="line"><!---->CWE-416 - Use After Free<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Details



<span class="line"><!---->Details<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Google Chrome is a cross-platform web browser, developed by Google.



<span class="line"><!---->Google Chrome is a cross-platform web browser, developed by Google.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Web Audio API is a high-level JavaScript API for processing and synthesizing audio in web applications. This advisory describes a vulnerability that happens in the Web Audio functionality of Chrome.



<span class="line"><!---->Web Audio API is a high-level JavaScript API for processing and synthesizing audio in web applications. This advisory describes a vulnerability that happens in the Web Audio functionality of Chrome.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





While running the supplied proof-of-concept, Chromium (ASAN version) crashes inside the blink::EventListenerMap::Remove function.



<span class="line"><!---->While running the supplied proof-of-concept, Chromium (ASAN version) crashes inside the blink::EventListenerMap::Remove function.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





As presented in the POC.HTML file:



<span class="line"><!---->As presented in the POC.HTML file:<!----></span>



<br>





Firstly, the AudioContext object will be created. Next the "flood" function executes. Registering an onstatechange event function will lead to infinite/extra iterations of "flood" function after another AudioContext object gets created, typically not more than max_num_output_streams (50 by default). During each "flood" function iteration, a new VIDEO element and an Oscillator audio node will be created. Eventually, the "flood" function execution will be interrupted by the meta refresh (which will reload the page every 3 seconds).



<span class="line"><!---->Firstly, the AudioContext object will be created. Next the "flood" function executes. Registering an onstatechange event function will lead to infinite/extra iterations of "flood" function after another AudioContext object gets created, typically not more than max_num_output_streams (50 by default). During each "flood" function iteration, a new VIDEO element and an Oscillator audio node will be created. Eventually, the "flood" function execution will be interrupted by the meta refresh (which will reload the page every 3 seconds).<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Due to the meta refresh (can be location.reload() or similar) the Frame/Context will be destroyed. During this context destruction the blink::MediaCustomControlsFullscreenDetector::Detach function will be executed (because the video control gets destroyed as well).



<span class="line"><!---->Due to the meta refresh (can be location.reload() or similar) the Frame/Context will be destroyed. During this context destruction the blink::MediaCustomControlsFullscreenDetector::Detach function will be executed (because the video control gets destroyed as well).<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This eventually (requires a few automatic page reloads - see meta refresh) will lead to a crash in the blink::EventListenerMap::Remove function. This bug happens because some of the registered event listeners at this point are no longer valid. And this situation is not properly handled in Chrome.



<span class="line"><!---->This eventually (requires a few automatic page reloads - see meta refresh) will lead to a crash in the blink::EventListenerMap::Remove function. This bug happens because some of the registered event listeners at this point are no longer valid. And this situation is not properly handled in Chrome.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





It is worth noting that after a slight PoC modification (i.e. removing the onstatechange event, and just executing the "flood" function directly) it is possible to cause the same issue in the blink::EventListenerMap::Add function. The culprit seems to be the same.



<span class="line"><!---->It is worth noting that after a slight PoC modification (i.e. removing the onstatechange event, and just executing the "flood" function directly) it is possible to cause the same issue in the blink::EventListenerMap::Add function. The culprit seems to be the same.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





In case of Chrome built from source (and the Canary version) the problem seems to be as follows:



<span class="line"><!---->In case of Chrome built from source (and the Canary version) the problem seems to be as follows:<!----></span>



<br>





The vulnerability triggers during heap garbage collection (e.g. can be triggered by removing/adding the video element). The invalid/corrupted element is added to the not_fully_constructed_worklist - which, as the name says, contains the list of objects that were not fully constructed. In order to add a new element to not_fully_constructed_worklist, Chrome executes the void MarkingWorklists::ExternalMarkingWorklist::Push(HeapObjectHeader* object) function.



<span class="line"><!---->The vulnerability triggers during heap garbage collection (e.g. can be triggered by removing/adding the video element). The invalid/corrupted element is added to the not_fully_constructed_worklist - which, as the name says, contains the list of objects that were not fully constructed. In order to add a new element to not_fully_constructed_worklist, Chrome executes the void MarkingWorklists::ExternalMarkingWorklist::Push(HeapObjectHeader* object) function.<!----></span>



<br>





Later, Chrome will try to mark all of the objects from not_fully_constructed_worklist in the MarkerBase::MarkNotFullyConstructedObjects(). causing an access violation due to the fact that one of the objects is invalid.



<span class="line"><!---->Later, Chrome will try to mark all of the objects from not_fully_constructed_worklist in the MarkerBase::MarkNotFullyConstructedObjects(). causing an access violation due to the fact that one of the objects is invalid.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>
